          <div class="small-text">
           <b>
            ADMINISTRATIVE CONTROLS
           </b>

          <div class="admin-ctl-btns whitebuttons-group">

          <div class="viewGalleryAdminActions small-text text-xs-small">

          <div class="tiny-text feature-status">
           Currently Featured in: US
          </div>

        <div class="hzTipBox invisibleBox" data-name="banner3" data-tip-id="3">
         <div class="tipBoxArrow" data-point-to="#hzEmbedBtn">
         </div>
         <div class="hzTipItem">
          Click "Embed" to display an article on your own website or blog.
          <a class="hzCloseTip hzi-font hzi-CloseX" href="javascript:;" title="Close">
          </a>

        <div class="viewGalleryDescriptionHolder" itemprop="description">
         <div class="viewGalleryDescription " id="viewGalleryDescription">
          A bathroom layout is mostly a pretty easy decision. If the plumbing is already in place and youre using standard-size pieces, like a typical 60-inch bathtub, there arent a whole lot of options for rearranging that floor plan. However, when bringing your dream design into the real world, you have to consider the third dimension and figure out what height is right for everything you bring into your room. Consider this your guide to hanging, installing and aligning the many small features of your bathroom.
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="out" id="gallerySpaces" itemprop="articleBody" lb-context="gallery_29060785" scopeid="gallerySpaces">
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="12402101" objid="12402101" posid="0">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/12402101/Wilton-Whole-Home-Renovation-transitional-bathroom-other-metro">
            <div>
             <img alt="Transitional Bathroom by Terracotta Design Build" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="639" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'12402101');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/ea615639037a6707_1485-w422-h639-b0-p0--transitional-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/12402101/Wilton-Whole-Home-Renovation-transitional-bathroom-other-metro">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/terracottadesignbuild/terracotta-design-build">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Terracotta Design Build
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="12402101">
            <b>
             Sinks
            </b>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            The counter height is typically 32 to 34 in., but whats actually more important is your sink height.
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="11871552" objid="11871552" posid="1">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/11871552/Tiled-Powder-Room-Robeson-Design-transitional-powder-room-san-diego">
            <div>
             <img alt="Transitional Powder Room by Robeson Design" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="639" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'11871552');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/f2818a24036ae6c1_8718-w422-h639-b0-p0--transitional-powder-room.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/11871552/Tiled-Powder-Room-Robeson-Design-transitional-powder-room-san-diego">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/rebeccarobeson/robeson-design">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Robeson Design
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="11871552">
            An above-counter vessel sink will naturally sit much higher than an inset below-counter sink, and so a vessel should be placed on a lowered cabinet to compensate. Ultimately, you should try a few different sinks (in store or in bathrooms you like) and figure out the height that feels most comfortable for you.
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="5177167" objid="5177167" posid="2">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/5177167/Potrero-HIll-eclectic-bathroom-san-francisco">
            <div>
             <img alt="Eclectic Bathroom by Antonio Martins Interior Design" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="634" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'5177167');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/80f16c490208eadf_2287-w422-h634-b0-p0--eclectic-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/5177167/Potrero-HIll-eclectic-bathroom-san-francisco">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/antoniomartins11/antonio-martins-interior-design">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Antonio Martins Interior Design
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="5177167">
            <b>
             Mirrors
            </b>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            Likewise, the height of mirrors should be based on your own height. Find an average eyeline for everyone using the mirrors and make sure this height is well within the upper and lower borders of the mirror (5 ft., 6
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            is average, but your household may vary).
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="4990370" objid="4990370" posid="3">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/4990370/Contemporary-Condo-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
            <div>
             <img alt="Contemporary Bathroom by Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="572" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'4990370');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/38e1178c01f96e5c_1217-w422-h572-b0-p0--contemporary-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/4990370/Contemporary-Condo-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/yanicsimard/toronto-interior-design-group-yanic-simard">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="4990370">
            In many situations a centerline can be created between the counter and the ceiling for the most symmetrical look. (Using this same centerline for sconces reinforces the effect, as seen here in one of my projects.)
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="5996624" objid="5996624" posid="4">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/5996624/Main-Line-PA-Powder-Room-transitional-powder-room-philadelphia">
            <div>
             <img alt="Transitional Powder Room by Rudloff Custom Builders" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="634" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'5996624');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/08d1270d024b097b_8794-w422-h634-b0-p0--transitional-powder-room.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/5996624/Main-Line-PA-Powder-Room-transitional-powder-room-philadelphia">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/rudloff4/rudloff-custom-builders">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Rudloff Custom Builders
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="5996624">
            People often place the bottom edge of the mirror above the faucet, but in fact allowing the two to visually overlap can create a very elegant effect.
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="3430236" objid="3430236" posid="5">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/3430236/Peninsula-Point-Residence-transitional-bathroom-orange-county">
            <div>
             <img alt="Transitional Bathroom by Eric Aust Architect" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="504" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'3430236');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/41f15089015b3eb3_2544-w422-h504-b0-p0--transitional-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/3430236/Peninsula-Point-Residence-transitional-bathroom-orange-county">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/ericaust/eric-aust-architect">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Eric Aust Architect
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="3430236">
            <b>
             Makeup Stations
            </b>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            When combining a standing vanity with a sit-down makeup station, youll need to adjust the height down to about 28
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            or lower (minimum: about 24
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            ).
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="517244" objid="517244" posid="6">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/517244/Andrea-May-Hunter-Gatherer-eclectic-bathroom-san-diego">
            <div>
             <img alt="Eclectic Bathroom by Andrea May Hunter/Gatherer" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="634" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'517244');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/73f1eb2c0f259be2_3304-w422-h634-b0-p0--eclectic-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/517244/Andrea-May-Hunter-Gatherer-eclectic-bathroom-san-diego">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/amayhg/andrea-may-hunter-gatherer">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Andrea May Hunter/Gatherer
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="517244">
            Try sitting at a real desk or vanity and see if it feels comfortable, considering youll be applying makeup rather than typing  going on the low side is better for leaning forward.
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container landscape " lb-sid="10668161" objid="10668161" posid="7">
          <div class="gallery-photo reloadMe trackMe" data-full="746,496" data-stnd="606,403">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/10668161/Condo-Renovation-Kitchen-and-Bath-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
            <div>
             <img alt="Contemporary Bathroom by Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard" class="hide-context reloadable" data-pin-no-hover="true" height="403" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'10668161');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/54b17c9e033c1bd1_1616-w606-h403-b0-p0--contemporary-bathroom.jpg" width="606"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/10668161/Condo-Renovation-Kitchen-and-Bath-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/yanicsimard/toronto-interior-design-group-yanic-simard">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="10668161">
            <b>
             Showers
            </b>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            <b>
             Enclosures.
            </b>
            I prefer to run shower enclosure glass to the full ceiling height (with the door just slightly below, to allow for a free swing), as I did in the bathroom shown here. An 18-
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            -wide fixed panel and a 24-
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            -wide door panel work well for a typical 60-
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            tub. Place the doorknob at about 36
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            off the floor or wherever is comfortable for you to reach. (Follow the placement of knobs in other rooms that work well for you.)
            <br/>
            <br/>
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/ideabooks/18668374/list/8-stunning-and-soothing-shower-designs" target="_blank">
             See
             <span>
              8 stunning and soothing shower designs
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="466288" objid="466288" posid="8">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/466288/Casa-Verde-Design-traditional-bathroom-minneapolis">
            <div>
             <img alt="Traditional Bathroom by Casa Verde Design" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="634" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'466288');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/f561b6c60f134559_6087-w422-h634-b0-p0--traditional-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/466288/Casa-Verde-Design-traditional-bathroom-minneapolis">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/casaverdedesign/casa-verde-design">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Casa Verde Design
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="466288">
            <b>
             Benches.
            </b>
            Shower benches have lots of practical uses, such as giving you a place to perch your leg when shaving. Thus, the top can sit a bit lower (16
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            ) than typical seat height.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/ideabooks/18219713/list/outfit-your-shower-with-the-right-bench-for-you" target="_blank">
             See more on shower benches
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="3987602" objid="3987602" posid="9">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/3987602/Eclectic-Bathroom-transitional-bathroom-chicago">
            <div>
             <img alt="Transitional Bathroom Eclectic Bathroom" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="634" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'3987602');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/71b1370f019b87e4_2452-w422-h634-b0-p0--transitional-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="3987602">
            <b>
             Showerheads.
            </b>
            A showerhead, even a rainshower one, shouldnt sit so low that you must crouch or so high that the water pelts you rather than gently raining down. A height of 6 ft., 6
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            is typical, but this can be adjusted for taller or shorter bathers. Also keep in mind that it must project far enough for you to stand under it, which is especially important to remember when you have a shower bench or a tub-shower combination.
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="8816022" objid="8816022" posid="10">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/8816022/San-Francisco-Urban-Contemporary-Design-transitional-bathroom">
            <div>
             <img alt="Transitional Bathroom by New Marble Company Inc." class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="634" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'8816022');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/9661d71c02f93460_1762-w422-h634-b0-p0--transitional-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/8816022/San-Francisco-Urban-Contemporary-Design-transitional-bathroom">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/newmarbleco/new-marble-company-inc">
             <span class="pro-name">
              New Marble Company Inc.
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="8816022">
            <b>
             Niches.
            </b>
            I love adding niches to shower areas, for the practical storage capabilities and the beautiful accent. For a tub they make sense just above the tub surface, as youll be lying down when you reach for that shampoo, but in a shower they should be much higher, around 48
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            , so you dont have to lean down to reach anything.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            Place your shower controls around 42 to 48
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            at the center, and a tub filler 4 to 6
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            above the top of the tub.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/ideabooks/5158473/list/how-to-pick-a-shower-niche-thats-not-stuck-in-a-rut" target="_blank">
             See more on shower niches
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="4616908" objid="4616908" posid="11">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/4616908/Bathroom-Project-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
            <div>
             <img alt="Contemporary Bathroom by Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="639" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'4616908');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/1191e0ba01dc16bf_8246-w422-h639-b0-p0--contemporary-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/4616908/Bathroom-Project-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/yanicsimard/toronto-interior-design-group-yanic-simard">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="4616908">
            <b>
             Toilet Paper Holders
            </b>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            When placing the paper holder, the tendency can be to picture the roll as hanging lower than it really should. Standard height is about 26
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            off the floor, which is closer to the height of the top of the tank than to the seat, so I recommend placing it on this level for a clean line, like Ive done in this bathroom. Attaching it to the side of the vanity (toward the front rather than centered, for reachability) is another option for tighter spaces.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/ideabooks/20422407/list/the-absolute-right-way-to-hang-toilet-paper-maybe" target="_blank">
             See the absolute right way to hang toilet paper
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="421727" objid="421727" posid="12">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/421727/Pleasant-Valley-transitional-bathroom-little-rock">
            <div>
             <img alt="Transitional Bathroom by Tobi Fairley Interior Design" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="634" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'421727');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/9be1cf950efb38e3_3379-w422-h634-b0-p0--transitional-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/421727/Pleasant-Valley-transitional-bathroom-little-rock">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/tobifairley/tobi-fairley-interior-design">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Tobi Fairley Interior Design
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="421727">
            <b>
             Towel Bars and Hooks
            </b>
            <br/>
            <br/>
            For other accessories, like towel hooks and robe hooks, the height is flexible, but consider the length of what will hang. Towels need at least 36
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
            typically; washcloths,
            <span>
             18
            </span>
            <span>
             in.;
            </span>
            and robes, 60
            <span>
             in.
            </span>
             its best not to eyeball it. A standard towel rail is 48 in. above the floor, but it can be adjusted to line up with something else (like the knob on the shower door or the towel hooks over the vanity) without being too hard to reach.
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallery-photo-container portrait " lb-sid="10668164" objid="10668164" posid="13">
          <div class="gallery-photo trackMe">
           <a compid="img" href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/10668164/Condo-Renovation-Kitchen-and-Bath-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
            <div>
             <img alt="Contemporary Bathroom by Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard" class="hide-context " data-pin-no-hover="true" height="639" lb-mag="" lb-view="" oncontextmenu="PhotoContextMenu.show(event,'10668164');return false;" ondragstart="return false" onmousedown="preventImageDrag(event)" onselectstart="return false" src="http://st.houzz.com/fimgs/c7e18708033c1bd9_8221-w422-h639-b0-p0--contemporary-bathroom.jpg" width="422"/>
            </div>
           </a>
           <div class="space-link tiny-text" compid="more">
            <a href="http://www.houzz.com/photos/10668164/Condo-Renovation-Kitchen-and-Bath-contemporary-bathroom-other-metro">
             <span class="more-icon">
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
           <div class="gallery-photo-credit tiny-text" compid="credit">
            <a class="hz-username" href="http://www.houzz.com/pro/yanicsimard/toronto-interior-design-group-yanic-simard">
             <span class="pro-name">
              Toronto Interior Design Group | Yanic Simard
             </span>
            </a>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="gallery-text">
           <div class="thBuzz" hid="10668164">
            <b>
             Designer secret:
            </b>
            One of the items that I found often goes the most overlooked in bathroom design is actually one that ironically is best left unseen: the electrical outlets.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            Here youll notice that the electrical for the vanity seems, well, to not exist at all. Thats because the outlet is actually tucked next to the vanity cabinet, just below the lower edge of the sink counter. This way its still conveniently positioned for plugging in a blow-dryer or electric shaver but is visually hidden from many angles.
            <br/>
            <br/>
            <b>
             More:
            </b>
            <span>
             <a href="http://www.houzz.com/ideabooks/26567086/list/key-measurements-to-make-the-most-of-your-bathroom" target="_blank">
              Key Measurements to Make the Most of Your Bathroom
             </a>
            </span>
           </div>
          </div>

           <div class="comment " data-hz='{"id":"568345"}'>
            <span class="anchorPoint" id="c3">
            </span>
            <a class="hlAnchor" name="568345">
            </a>
            <div class="flag-message text-center">
             Thank you for reporting this comment.
             <a class="flag-comment-action colorLink unflag" href="javascript:">
              Undo
             </a>
            </div>
            <div class="feedUThumb pull-left mrm">
             <img class="hzHouzzer hzHCUserImage userImage hz-user-image" data-id="sauveteur" data-type="profile" src="http://st.houzz.com/simgs/266307760f70245d_0-9405/sauveteur.jpg"/>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-actions">
            </div>
            <div class="commentBody">
             <div class="commentBodyContent">
              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="sauveteur" data-type="profile">
               Sauve
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               I am short, petite at 5'1", although I always lied and told everyone I was 5'2" if they asked me. So I find built-ins in any room meant for giants of 5'7" to 6'. That's probably why I detest built-ins anywhere. But the bathroom is really my pet peeve since it is so difficult to change. What I have found over the years is this. Unless a man lather and shaves, other than brushing his teeth, he seldom uses the bathroom sink for much else. I, and the women I know, use the sink for washing our face at least twice a day and during the summer it can be often twice a day. After having 2 daughters, both of whom I taught the essential of rinsing with clear water 20 times, there's always a small flood on the surrounding floor in a single sink vanity with the oval bowl set into the top. All fine and good, quick mop up with a towel. But when the sink is on top of the vanity it is a disaster. Water everywhere and often dripping onto the vanity's front and sides all the way down to puddling on the floor. We lived in an apartment that had twin above the vanity bathroom sinks that were each larger than the sink in the kitchen. I had to stand on a step stool to use one to wash my face or there would be water not only on and down the front of the cabinet to floor but also all my front body. So I would like to suggest to all architects, contractors, and renovators: If you know the persons your are working with then it is a good idea to ask them to consider the manner in which they use the bathroom sink. For me, I don't want to have to climb on a foot-stool to wash my face, ever.
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="commentInfo tiny-text">
              <span class="likeContainer">
               <a class="like" data-object-id="568345" data-object-type="9" data-self="0" href="#" title="Like">

               </a>

              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="evil_overlord" data-type="profile">
               evil_overlord
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               Arranging the mirror for an average height is a &lt;i&gt;_terrible_&lt;/i&gt; idea. What you want is a mirror tall enough to accommodate _all_ the heights of potential users. In our case, I'm 6'4", my wife is 5'4"; average would be 5'10". Average usually means I can see my chin if I'm lucky.  Instead of aiming for that average, we got tall mirrors that suit her and me equally. We also have dual sinks at substantially different heights; it looks odd, but works really well. No stretching for her, no more back pain for me.
              </div>
             </div>

              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="kat_sheridan" data-type="profile">
               Kat Sheridan
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               If you're going to the expense of remodeling, take the time to build for future disabilities. An accident left me in a wheelchair for a few months and gave me plenty of opportunity to discover that "normal height" is no use when seated. Those lovely raised sinks can't be leaned over from a seated height. Mirrors suddenly only show your forehead. You can't lean across the vanity top. That lovely lowered makeup vanity shown above would be much better if it included a small sink, even off to one side. Lots of women use water as they make up (to wash hands, wash off make up, wet certain kinds of makeup, etc.), and it becomes a good place to easily accomodate someone with an unexpected disability since you can pull a wheelchair up under it, the mirror is lower, etc. Just one extra small sink would make a big difference.
              </div>
             </div>

              <div class="commentBodyText">
               What I'm seeing in the comments so far, mirrors (pun!) my experience.
               <br/>
               It seems we all customize our fixture/counter heights.
               <br/>
               I'm 5'10" and my girlfriend at the time of my last house reno stood 4'9".
               <br/>
               I had everything built a few inches below standard so that she would not have to resort to step stools and stretching up on her tip-toes as she had done her whole life. I made a long, tall bathroom mirror running from just about the sink lip to 7 feet on the wall to accommodate everyone except professional basketball players.
               <br/>
               She loves to cook, so I carried the lower counter heights  through to the kitchen, too.
               <br/>
               Her back pain issues lessened significantly in our time in that house.
              </div>

              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="leslieg2013" data-type="profile">
               leslieg2013
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               IMHO it is counterproductive to title an article, "The Right Height for . . . " when in actuality, the "right height" is the height that works best for the individual(s).
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Getting your bathroom fixtures "right" requires thought, planning and detailed measuring.  Doing a full scale mock-up of your layout is often necessary.  This takes time and a willingness to participate in the process.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Houzz is, I think, the best design website out there. But if your are coming to Houzz for easy answers, you have come to the wrong place.
              </div>
             </div>

              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="jmpjmp" data-type="profile">
               jmpjmp
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               Lots of good advice.  Here are a few of my thoughts, based on our own recent renovation:
               <br/>
               <br/>
               If niches are tucked into a wall so as to be invisible from outside the shower, the inevitable mess is invisible too.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Putting an outlet inside vanity cabinets allows rechargeable razors and toothbrushes to remain hidden while recharging.  These would be in addition to the more usual GFCI outlets nearby.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Lights on the side of vanity mirrors should not be too low or they will cause uncomfortable glare and not illuminate the face well.  The bulbs should not be the filament types which have blinding glare.  This is a great place for a dimmer as well.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               A heated floor or heated towel rack is a wonderful thing for a bath, both for comfort and for reducing dampness.  In a bath these are not very expensive if done during a renovation.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Always remember storage, either under the sink(s) if not pedestals or in a small closet.
              </div>
             </div>

             <img class="hzHouzzer hzHCUserImage userImage hz-user-image" data-id="smallhousegirl" data-type="profile" src="http://www.houzz.com/res/2199/pic/user_0.png?v=2199"/>
             <div class="hzProIndicator text-center text-bold text-xs-xsmall">
              PRO
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-actions">
            </div>
            <div class="commentBody">
             <div class="commentBodyContent">
              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="smallhousegirl" data-type="profile">
               The Big Small
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               Great article with loads of standard heights that we too use as a starting point.  Very handy!  One addition that isn't really to do with height, but more the placement of shower niches.  First....I love niches - they give showers a custom look, but more importantly, give the clutter of bottles and soaps a place to call home.  Generally we steer clients away from placing a niche close to the shower head as the joints between the niche and surrounding cement/glass faced board are notoriously difficult to waterproof.  Not impossible, but difficult.  Thus, best kept away from the splash zone of the shower.  It is getting easier now with ready-made niches that come pre-waterproofed and tile ready, but for peace of mind, I usually suggest the wall opposite the shower head.  Having torn out a number of older showers, I've seen the more than my share of leaks at niches...with the associated mould.  Of course you can put a niche anywhere in the shower (for example under the shower head as seen in the photo above), but you need to have absolute confidence that the installer waterproofing the niche prior to tile application knows what they are doing, and that your tile setter slopes the horizontal surface that shampoos etc will sit on adequately so excess water drains off into the shower and doesn't sit in the niche.
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="commentInfo tiny-text">
              <span class="likeContainer">
               <a class="like" data-object-id="569513" data-object-type="9" data-self="0" href="#" title="Like">

              <div class="commentBodyText">
               Currently building a new house in Laos (with building issues that most readers here could not fathom). Without digressing from this topic, I'm 6 feet tall and my wife is 4 ft 9. Trying to figure out the best height that would work for both of us is a challenge. Installing duel height vanities. Kitchen counter height will be suitable for me since Laotians prefer to work crouching off the floor, though, with an island, will also have duel work heights.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               As an aside, building in a country where design is virtually non-existent is quite a task. The workers, who barely understand basic construction techniques, have no concept of why you might want to create something beautiful and unusual. Maybe one day I'll post an article on building a concept design house in a least-developed country.

              <div class="commentBodyText">
               TIP:  If you are unusually tall or short, try to hire a designer or architect who is about your height. They will have experienced your issues and know the pain.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               My really tall BIL did a bathroom remodel for a professional basketball player, who looked at him when they met, was not looking down at the top of his head, and hired him on the spot because there would be no push-back over the need for over-sized and over-height design details.

            <span class="anchorPoint" id="c42">
            </span>
            <a class="hlAnchor" name="569704">
            </a>
            <div class="flag-message text-center">
             Thank you for reporting this comment.
             <a class="flag-comment-action colorLink unflag" href="javascript:">

            <div class="feedUThumb pull-left mrm">
             <img class="hzHouzzer hzHCUserImage userImage hz-user-image" data-id="evil_overlord" data-type="profile" src="http://www.houzz.com/res/2199/pic/user_0.png?v=2199"/>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-actions">
            </div>
            <div class="commentBody">
             <div class="commentBodyContent">
              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="evil_overlord" data-type="profile">
               evil_overlord
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               @curlieq
               <br/>
               You have to decide how long you'll retain the house. We built this house for ourselves, for long-term use. Because of that, we felt free to make choices that worked best for us, without caring too much about re-sale. Some of the choices we made, that might benefit you:
               <br/>
               <br/>
               1. Master bathroom sinks. Two side-by-side/connected vanities, one convenient for her, one convenient for me; there's a good 6-8" difference, I think. They look decidedly odd at first, but they're very comfortable to use - I no longer have to bend over all the time.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               2. Master bathroom shower. We built a double-wide shower. Her 'side' has a telephone shower with the head generally set pretty low. Mine is a fixed shower head at about 7'6" or 8'. Both of us are comfortable; great solution if you have the space. Also, the door to the shower is 'borderless' - there's no rail above for stability. These rails are the bane my existence in hotels and guest rooms; I often hit my head. Lack of a rail means the side panels need extra support.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               3. Kitchen counters. Happily for me, my wife does most of the cooking. Kitchen counters are therefore mostly at 'her' height. However, there's a section raised by 2"-3" that I can work at when I'm helping. This higher section is also a breakfast bar on the other side, so the height works well for that too.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               4. Windows. If you're building your house, take the chance to make the windows work for both. This is one place we miscalculated - misunderstanding that a 7 foot 'head' meant the top of the opening, without trim. So the installed windows feel a little low for me, but really only because we have an open plan. Close up, the glass is still above my eyes.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               5. Cabinets. We took advantage of my height to have some storage space that's quite high up. When I'm home, I can reach; when I'm not, my wife needs a stepladder, but we use the space for items we rarely use.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               6. Bathtub. This was surprisingly difficult to find; I wanted a soaking tub long enough to really relax and read in, but narrow (since we're both thin), and without any jets, etc. American 'soaking' tubs tend to get really, really wide, and have jets built in. We finally bought a German tub, which was so expensive that we joke about amortizing the cost every time we use it. I love baths, so it was worth the cost, but for most people it might not be. It's also less comfortable for my wife to use, since she has nothing to brace against - she could basically lie flat on the base of the tub. Like the kitchen, this was one area where we designed primarily for the key user. ( I know; i take the baths, she does the cooking. Doesn't seem fair. )
               <br/>
               <br/>
               7. Toilet. There's not much choice in toilet heights, but we chose tall ones. More comfortable for me, not uncomfortable for her.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               For guest rooms, and for all mirrors, we took everybody's height into account. The family includes both tall and short, so we made the guest vanity a normal height, the guest shower a telephone shower that can accommodate everyone, and all mirrors pretty much from the top of the vanity to over my head. In the master bath, that's quite a lot of mirror, but we used borderless mirrors that work, look good, and make the room feel bigger.
              </div>
             </div>

              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="smallhousegirl" data-type="profile">
               The Big Small
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               @ann danielson - a good question with an historical answer.   The majority of homes made in the post war boom in North America were small by today's standards, and a 3 bedroom, 1 bathroom home was a very common configuration.  In this situation, designers were accounting for the likelihood that the single bathroom would be used by both adults and children.  Thus bath counters of 30-32" became the norm.  I wholeheartedly agree that this is uncomfortably low for many adults and not needed in every bath in the home.  We now make our vanities higher in master baths (34-36" depending owner preference) and go with 31-33" in a baths potentially used by children.
              </div>
             </div>

              <div class="commentBodyText">
               @Ann Danielson Bathroom counters were lowered so that kids can use them.  Recently, it's become more common to see bathroom counters at the same height (36").  This is called Comfort Height.  Standard Vanity Height is 32" and this is probably what you're used to.   Here:
               <br/>
               <br/>
               http://www.tradewindsimports.com/blog/misc/comfort-height-bathroom-vanities/
               <br/>
               <br/>
               @The Big Small that's great historical insight.  I always advise to go with Comfort Height Cabinets.  Your back will love you for it.
              </div>

               Great practical advice; this is the kind of information that is often omitted in design but when ignored, makes for irritating daily experiences. Thank you for the emphasis on personal preference. I have stayed in remodeled hotel rooms where the modern vanity was obviously designed for a tall guy and I could, at 5'6", barely reach the faucets or see in the vanity mirror. "Just right" varies and a range of options is extremely useful. Thanks for a great article!

              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="victoran" data-type="profile">
               victoran
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               Another height idea for a shower is to have a rain shower (heaven) that has a bar connecting it to the wall on a sliding ring.  In France, many showers have this as well as the Presidio in San Francisco. Sorry, no photo.
               <br/>
               It was wonderful, as being short, I just moved the bar down to my height while my husband moved it up to its full height.  The shower also had not only rain shower, but also traditional hand held shower. Nice to have all the options.  When we move, we will have a walk-in (wheelchair roll in ) access with seat and rain shower and hand held...Comfort is the #1 issue in a good shower design.
              </div>
             </div>

            <div class="feedUThumb pull-left mrm">
             <img class="hzHouzzer hzHCUserImage userImage hz-user-image" data-id="timothyschultz" data-type="profile" src="http://st.houzz.com/simgs/31c3710d002b091e_0-5748/timothyschultz.jpg"/>
             <div class="hzProIndicator text-center text-bold text-xs-xsmall">
              PRO
             </div>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-actions">
            </div>
            <div class="commentBody">
             <div class="commentBodyContent">
              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="timothyschultz" data-type="profile">
               Seattle Custom Cabinets
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               In order to receive a building permit the architect should be required to demonstrate they can get all the way from an automobile into a shower or bathtub with a wheelchair or walker.  It's pretty stupid to end up prematurely in an assisted living situation merely because you can't take a bath.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Showers should have really solid grab rails for safety and/or recreation.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Showers should have a place to sit down to wash your feet or shave your legs.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               Two shower heads are a must, especially if you shower by yourself.
               <br/>
               Once you shower with two heads every other shower you take will be lacking in quality.
               <br/>
               Five heads are better than two.  Showers are one of the best parts of the day.
               <br/>
               You should treat yourself.
               <br/>
               <br/>
               <br/>
              </div>
             </div>

            <div class="feedUThumb pull-left mrm">
             <img class="hzHouzzer hzHCUserImage userImage hz-user-image" data-id="veejayzed" data-type="profile" src="http://www.houzz.com/res/2199/pic/user_0.png?v=2199"/>

            <div class="comment-actions">
            </div>
            <div class="commentBody">
             <div class="commentBodyContent">
              <span class="hz-username hzHouzzer hzHCUserName " data-id="veejayzed" data-type="profile">
               veejayzed
              </span>
              <div class="commentBodyText">
               <p>
                Great article and helpful! I like your thoughts &amp; pictures of the seated make-up station beside the sink vanity. I don't like doing anything over the sink which is why I've always thought two sinks is a waste of space. I also don't want anyone in the bathroom with me, so my husband and I use it in order - get in and out. Because of that and finding it unpleasant to stay in the steamy bathroom to do make-up or hair - generally I've set up a station at a desk, or a place to stand in front of a wall mirror (so I can get close enough to actually see) in the bedroom. BUT,  Paul's comment above reminds me there is a place for it - if there are significant height differences in the users...Lots of good thoughts on placing outlets too!
               </p>
               <p>
                Wondering if anyone else hates conventional toilet paper holders?  You can't use them one-handed anyway, they are too fiddly to install and change out the roll which also has to be done too often...I like the vertical ones I've seen lately - just drop it onto the spindle. I'm building a new bath in a small house and I've got the most narrow space possible for the toilet anyway - so I plan to build a niche right beside to hold several rolls.
               </p>
              </div>
             </div>

			return data[0] + "=" + data[2] + data[1];
